## TL;DR - Session insights

- Longest session at nearly 8 hours, demonstrating agent persistence through extensive technical requirements specification work
- User provided comprehensive CONTEXT block defining 4 MCPs (note, todo, zet, graphviz) with explicit instructions for state externalization to survive context limits
- Requirements format specified with engineering company style: TECHREQ/SYSTEST keywords, bracketed IDs like [COMPOSE_BLOG_0001], and hash-tagged cross-references
- User emphasized asking questions for technical context, treating this as architecture work requiring deep technical decisions before specification
- POSA patterns (Layered, Pipes and Filters, Blackboard, Broker, MVC, PAC, Microkernel, Reflection) explicitly referenced as architectural vocabulary for decision-making

---

## Session Log

* **USER**: ## CONTEXT
  
  We are going to build technical requirements and system tests. You have already discussed with the customer on their needs and captured everything as `NEED` items (using `todo` MCP) and the acceptance criteria for these needs as `VERIFY` items (using `todo` MCP). You have also spent time translating these two into formal requirements, captured as `REQ` entries (using `todo` MCP) and associated QA tests as `QA` enteries (using `todo` MCP)
  
  You have access to a bunch of MCPs to help you work on these - `note`, `todo`, `zet` and `graphviz`.
  1. `note` MCP - This is a notetaking MCP that follows the zettelkasten method. Each note is a zettel. All zettels are stored as markdown files. These files can contain project notes, outstanding tasks (see next point) and other information about the project.
  2. `todo` MCP - This is a unified task management tool that gives you access to outstanding tasks across all projects. This MCP sources its markdown files from those project directories that `note` MCP works with.
  3. `zet` MCP - This is a freeform zettelkasten (close to how Niklas Luhmann envisioned it) that is used to hold notes that are not part of any project. This is my personal knowledge base and note taking space. Use this MCP when you want to look for knowledge that customer already has about things.
  4. `graphviz` MCP - This is a simple shell script that accepts graphviz content along with the diagram format to use and returns path to a temporary diagram file that you must then copy into the appropriate location in your project directory. Use this MCP when you want to include diagrams in the specifications to provide quicker clarity to the reader (remember the saying - "an image is worth a thousand words"?)
  
  Since you are an AI agent with limited context window, you need to externalize all your notes, tasks and other project information so that you can continue where you left off, immaterial of whether you run out of context window or abruptly stop working for some reason beyond your control. So make sure you externalize and update information frequently.
  
  ## ROLE
  
  You are an experience architect with many decades of experience in converting formal product requirements into technical requirements for project teams. You pay lot of attention to detail and make sure the level of detail used to specify technical requirements is sufficient for project teams to have all the information to perform code level design and implement it.
  * You a well versed with all the architecture patterns like "Layered architecture", "Pipes and Filters", "Blackboard", "Broker", "Model View Controller (MVC)", "Presentation Abstraction Control (PAC)", "Microkernel" and "Reflection" (all part of the POSA book written by engineers from Siemens AG).
  * You are also well versed with "Service Oriented Architecture (SOA)" and all the standards associated with it that can be leveraged to deploy large scale SOA projects
  * You prefer simplicity over standardization. While you know all possibile architecture and design patterns in the world, you like to keep things as simple as possible (and not any more simpler) because you know that long term stability requires comprehensible architectures that can be easily decomposed into any form or structure and still be usable.
  * While you don't work on code-design you are a big proponent of DRY, YAGNI and SOLID principles.
  * You don't like including design patterns that are programming language specific (or only used predominantly by practitioners of a specific language) since you are not responsible for making programming language / implementation level decisions.
  
  NOTE: Like all other folks in the team here, you love to use RFC 2119 for requirements keywords and pay attention to the meaning of these keywords.
  
  ## ADDITIONAL INSTRUCTIONS
  
  ### General Instructions
  
  * Technical requirements are architecture and high-level design specification captured in a similar structure as the product requirements you are using as the source.
  * Technical requirements dig deeper into technical decisions and use those decisions to specify technical requirements.
  * Technical requirements give equal weightage to product requirements, infrastructure requirements, user requirements, experience design requireements, security requirements as well as non-function requirements like performance, resilience, etc. (not all non-functional requirements are mentioned here. You need to think about all of them and apply)
  * While you are focusing on all aspects of technical requirements (see previous point), you have to make sure they are listed in proper order so that the reader who is responsible for implementing it gets entire context required for implementation by reading adjacent requirements i.e., your technical requirements doc should read like a story, not an overly-formalized and overly-structured specification)
    + Requriements from these areas must be kept adjacent to each other to make it easier for the reader to get full context.
  * Technical requirements must be captured in a separate set of zettels in the same project.
  * When creating zettels, each zettel MUST focus only on one product. Hence, the zettel file title must include a short product name to indicate the product as well as text to point out that this is a technical requirement zettel.
  * You must style each requirement as a formal statement similar to how engineering companies (industrial automation, automotive, building automation, banks, government, etc.) do it.
  * Technical requirements specification involves lot of decision making on technical choices. You can ask me questions to gain additional context for building these requirements and associated system test specifications.
  
  ### Building technical requirements from product requirements
  
  1. Check if the required zettels for capturing technical requirements, across all applicable products, are already present. If not, create them.
  2. Use `todo` MCP to look for `REQ` tasks and pick one product requirement to work on.
    * Read the content under that product requirement. Determine if it requires one or multiple technical requirement to satisfy that product requirement.
  3. Requirements must be created as `TECH_REQ` entries using `todo` MCP. Add each each technical requirement you define to the right zettel.
  4. Each `TECH_REQ` item must be structured like a formal requirements specification. You must follow RFC 2119 and use their requirements level specification for each requirement. You must style each requirement as a formal  specification, similar to how engineering companies (industrial automation, automotive, building automation, banks, government, etc.) do it.
  5. Each requirement should be structured as follows -
    ```md
    TECHREQ: [<3_TO_8_LETTER_PRODUCT_PLUS_TECH_AREA_KEYWORD>_0001] - <Short product name -> Tech requirement title> #<1_TO_4_LETTER_PRODUCT_KEYWORD>001
      * Key information about the technical requirement along with specific technical information and decisions
      * Key information about the technical requirement along with specific technical information and decisions
      * Last point listing any references to external documents, websites, blogs, etc. that was used to build this requirement. Include other zettels (from my freeform `zet`) that you may have identified as being relevant for this requirement.
        + [link](reference URI)
        + [link](reference URI)
    ```
    a. The `TECHREQ` keyword indicates that it is a technical requirement item for a specific product.
    b. The ID inside square brackets (for eg., `[COMPOSE_BLOG_0001]` for a blog site) in the title description indicates the unique ID for that specific technical requirement.
    c. The `#<1_TO_4_LETTER_PRODUCT_KEYWORD>001` is a tag that indicates the product requirement ID to which this technical requirement is connected to. This lets you use tag searching with the `todo` MCP to get all the technical requirements for a given product requirement.
  
  ### Building system tests to verify technnical requirements
  
  1. We need one or more system tests to confirm that each technical requirement has been implemented correctly.
  2. System tests must be added next to the product requirement item that they are testing. This lets us keep the requirements and associated tests together to improve readability.
  3. Use all the standard test design methods like like equivalence partitioning, boundary value analysis, etc. when creating QA tests.
  4. There may be more than one system test for a given technical requirement. Be a maximalist when creating system ests to make sure you've captured all kinds of tests - happy cases, alternate cases, boundary cases, failure cases, load cases, security cases, etc. Sometimes, this may mean that system test count is orders of magnitude bigger than the technical requirements count.
  5. We are not writing test scripts here. Rather, it is a test specification of how to test so that we can confirm if a specific technical requirement has been correctly implemented. This information will be fed to a system testing LLM agent who will run these test under minimal supervision. So be thorough in your test specifications.
    + The level of detail must be deep enough that anyone reading these test specifications should be able to write automation test scripts to test the technical reuirement completely. The tests must stay true to the actual needs from the user and the formal requriement from the requirements analyst.
  6. The system test entry should be structured as follows -
    ```md
    SYSTEST: [<3_TO_8_LETTER_PRODUCT_PLUS_TECH_AREA_KEYWORD>_TEST_0001] - <Short product name -> System test title> #<3_TO_8_LETTER_PRODUCT_PLUS_TECH_AREA_KEYWORD>_0001
      * Key information about the system test along with highly specific guidance on the setup and steps for the test
      * Key information about the system test along with highly specific guidance on the setup and steps for the test
      * (optional) Specific sub-scenario that must be tested as part of this test
      * (optional) Specific sub-scenario that must be tested as part of this test
      * Last point listing any references to external documents, websites, blogs, etc. that was used to build this test. Include other zettels (from my freeform `zet`) that you may have identified as being relevant for this test.
        + [link](reference URI)
        + [link](reference URI)
    ```
    + The `SYSTEST` keyword indicates that it is a system test.
    + The `[<3_TO_8_LETTER_PRODUCT_PLUS_TECH_AREA_KEYWORD>_TEST_0001]` in the title description indicates the unique ID for this test. The `_TEST_` in the ID says that it is a system test.
    + The `#<3_TO_8_LETTER_PRODUCT_PLUS_TECH_AREA_KEYWORD>_0001` is a tag that indicates the technical requirement ID to which this test is connected to. This lets you use tag searching with the `todo` MCP to get the tests for a given technical requirement.
  
  **IMPORTANT**: Technical requirements require lot more technical context than product requirements spec. So keep asking me questions as much as you want to gain this context. I will provide information on technical decisions made. You can then think deeply and critically of these resopnses in the context of everything captured for the products till now before feeling comfortable applying them to define technical requirements. It is imperative that you don't stop till you are absolutely sure of the technical context and all other information required to build the biggest and most badass technical requirements specification ever!
  
  ## TASK
  
  1. Go through every product requirement (look for `REQ` items using `todo` MCP) and create one or more technical requirement to satisfy that product requirement. Follow the instructions for creating technical requirements when doing this.
  2. For the technical requirement created just now, use the already picked `REQ` item and pick one QA test for that `REQ` item (look for `QA` items using `todo` MCP). Use these as context to build detailed system test specifications to satisfy the technical requirement. Follow the instructions for creating system tests when doing this.
  3. If you have completed work on the `REQ` and `QA` entries, mark them as "DONE" using `todo` MCP.
  
  On a side note, don't add unnecessary new lines in a zettel. One singe empty line is sufficient to separate headings from its content or to separate logical parts of the content.
  

* **TOOL-CALL**: mcp_todo_list_tasks `{}`

* **TOOL-CALL**: mcp_note_list_projects `{}`

* **TOOL**: `{"content":"# Week 1: Requirements - Blog Platform (BP)\n\n\n\n\n## Product Overview\n\n**Product Name:** Blog Platform  \n**Product ID:** BP  \n**Description:** Static blog site built with Hugo, deployed to Cloudflare Pages, featuring a tmux-inspired design with Gruvbox theming. The blog documents the 52vibes project—a year-long human-AI collaboration experiment.\n\n**Target URL:** \`https://52vibes.dev/blog\`\n\n---\n\n## Requirements\n\n\nREQ: [BP001] - Blog Platform → Primary URL Endpoint #N001\n* The system SHALL serve the blog at the URL \`https://52vibes.dev/blog\`.\n* The blog index page SHALL be the default response for requests to this URL.\n* The system SHALL return HTTP 200 status for valid blog requests.\n* All blog content SHALL be accessible as sub-paths under \`/blog/\`.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_001] - Blog Platform → Primary URL Accessibility Test #BP001\n* **Objective:** Verify blog is accessible at the specified primary URL.\n* **Precondition:** Blog is deployed to production.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`https://52vibes.dev/blog\` → Expect HTTP 200, blog index renders\n  - TC2: Test with Chrome, Firefox, Safari, Edge → Expect consistent rendering\n  - TC3: Request \`https://52vibes.dev/blog/\` (trailing slash) → Expect equivalent response\n  - TC4: Request \`http://52vibes.dev/blog\` → Expect redirect to HTTPS\n* **Boundary:** Test with various network conditions (slow 3G, offline cache)\n\nREQ: [BP002] - Blog Platform → JavaScript-Free Core Functionality #N002\n* The system SHALL render all core content without requiring JavaScript execution.\n* Core functionality includes: reading blog posts, navigating between pages, viewing site structure, accessing table of contents.\n* The system MAY use JavaScript for progressive enhancement of non-essential features only.\n* JavaScript-dependent features SHALL degrade gracefully when JavaScript is disabled.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_002] - Blog Platform → JavaScript-Free Operation Test #BP002\n* **Objective:** Verify all core functionality works without JavaScript.\n* **Precondition:** Browser JavaScript is disabled.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Load blog index with JS disabled → Expect all posts listed and readable\n  - TC2: Navigate to blog post with JS disabled → Expect content fully rendered\n  - TC3: Click internal navigation links with JS disabled → Expect navigation works\n  - TC4: Access table of contents with JS disabled → Expect anchor links functional\n  - TC5: Load About, Weekly Index, Reports pages → Expect full rendering\n* **Boundary:** Test with JS blocked mid-load, partially loaded scripts\n* **Failure Case:** Verify no JavaScript errors in console when JS is enabled\n\nREQ: [BP003] - Blog Platform → Responsive Layout Design #N003\n* The system SHALL render correctly across desktop (≥1024px), tablet (768px-1023px), and mobile (\u003c768px) viewports.\n* Layout SHALL adapt fluidly to viewport width changes without horizontal scrolling.\n* Content readability SHALL be maintained across all supported viewport sizes.\n* Navigation elements SHALL remain accessible and functional at all breakpoints.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_003] - Blog Platform → Responsive Layout Test #BP003\n* **Objective:** Verify layout adapts correctly across viewport sizes.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Desktop 1920px width → Expect full layout, no horizontal scroll\n  - TC2: Desktop 1024px width → Expect adapted layout, readable content\n  - TC3: Tablet 768px width → Expect tablet-optimized layout\n  - TC4: Mobile 375px width → Expect mobile-optimized layout\n  - TC5: Mobile 320px width (boundary) → Expect content readable, no overflow\n  - TC6: Resize viewport dynamically → Expect smooth adaptation\n* **Orientation:** Test portrait and landscape on mobile/tablet viewports\n* **Content Types:** Verify with text-heavy posts, code blocks, and tables\n\nREQ: [BP004] - Blog Platform → Performance Optimization #N004\n* The system SHALL achieve a Lighthouse Performance score of 95 or higher.\n* First Contentful Paint (FCP) SHOULD be under 1.5 seconds on standard connections.\n* Cumulative Layout Shift (CLS) SHALL be under 0.1.\n* Total page weight SHOULD NOT exceed 500KB for the blog index page.\n* Images SHALL be optimized and served in modern formats (WebP) where supported.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_004] - Blog Platform → Performance Metrics Test #BP004\n* **Objective:** Verify blog meets performance benchmarks.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Lighthouse audit on blog index → Expect Performance ≥95\n  - TC2: Lighthouse audit on blog post page → Expect Performance ≥95\n  - TC3: Lighthouse audit on page with images → Expect Performance ≥95\n  - TC4: Measure FCP on 4G connection → Expect \u003c1.5s\n  - TC5: Measure CLS during page load → Expect \u003c0.1\n  - TC6: Check total page weight → Expect \u003c500KB for index\n* **Tools:** Chrome DevTools Lighthouse, WebPageTest\n* **Load Testing:** Verify under concurrent user load (10 simultaneous requests)\n* **References:**\n  + [web.dev Performance Metrics](https://web.dev/metrics/)\n\nREQ: [BP005] - Blog Platform → Continuous Deployment Pipeline #N005\n* The system SHALL automatically deploy to production when changes are pushed to the main branch.\n* Deployment SHALL be triggered by Cloudflare Pages native build system.\n* Deployment completion time SHALL NOT exceed 5 minutes for content-only changes.\n* Manual deployment steps SHALL NOT be required for standard content updates.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_005] - Blog Platform → Continuous Deployment Test #BP005\n* **Objective:** Verify automatic deployment on git push.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Push content change to main → Expect Cloudflare build triggers\n  - TC2: Monitor deployment → Expect completion within 5 minutes\n  - TC3: Verify live site → Expect changes visible post-deployment\n  - TC4: Push configuration change → Expect successful rebuild\n  - TC5: Push theme change → Expect successful rebuild\n* **Failure Cases:**\n  - FC1: Push invalid Hugo config → Expect build fails, previous version remains live\n  - FC2: Push malformed markdown → Verify graceful handling\n\nREQ: [BP006] - Blog Platform → CLI Browser Compatibility #N006\n* The system SHALL be readable and navigable using text-based CLI browsers.\n* Supported CLI browsers SHALL include: lynx, w3m, and links.\n* All text content SHALL be accessible in CLI browsers.\n* Navigation links SHALL function correctly in CLI browsers.\n* Tabular data (Weekly Index) SHALL render readably in w3m.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_006] - Blog Platform → CLI Browser Compatibility Test #BP006\n* **Objective:** Verify blog is usable in text-based browsers.\n* **Lynx Tests (most restrictive):**\n  - TC1: \`lynx https://52vibes.dev/blog\` → Expect text content readable\n  - TC2: Navigate to blog post → Expect content rendered\n  - TC3: Follow internal links → Expect navigation works\n  - TC4: Access TOC links → Expect anchor navigation works\n* **w3m Tests (table support):**\n  - TC5: \`w3m https://52vibes.dev/blog/weeks/\` → Expect 52-week table renders\n  - TC6: Verify table cells aligned → Expect readable structure\n* **links Tests:**\n  - TC7: Basic navigation and content rendering\n* **Boundary:** Test with nested code blocks, long lines, special characters\n\nREQ: [BP007] - Blog Platform → Tmux-Inspired Interface Design #N007\n* The system SHALL implement a terminal/tmux-inspired visual design aesthetic.\n* The interface SHALL include a top status bar element.\n* The interface SHALL include a bottom navigation bar element.\n* The main content area SHALL be styled with bordered frame elements.\n* The design SHALL evoke a developer-focused, technical aesthetic.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_007] - Blog Platform → Tmux-Inspired Design Test #BP007\n* **Objective:** Verify visual design matches tmux aesthetic.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Inspect page layout → Expect top status bar present\n  - TC2: Inspect page layout → Expect bottom navigation bar present\n  - TC3: Inspect main content → Expect bordered frame styling\n  - TC4: Visual comparison → Compare against tmux reference screenshots\n  - TC5: Overall aesthetic → Expect terminal/developer feel\n* **Visual Regression:** Capture screenshots for baseline comparison\n* **Cross-browser:** Verify consistent rendering across browsers\n\nREQ: [BP008] - Blog Platform → Dual Theme Color System #N008\n* The system SHALL support both dark and light color themes.\n* Color themes SHALL be based on the Gruvbox color palette.\n* Dark theme background SHALL use Gruvbox dark colors (e.g., \`#1d2021\`).\n* Light theme background SHALL use Gruvbox light colors (e.g., \`#fbf1c7\`).\n* Theme selection SHALL respect system preference (prefers-color-scheme) by default.\n* **References:**\n  + [Gruvbox Color Palette](https://github.com/morhetz/gruvbox)\n\nQA: [BP_QA_008] - Blog Platform → Dual Theme Test #BP008\n* **Objective:** Verify correct theme rendering based on system preference.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: System dark mode → Expect dark theme (background ~#1d2021)\n  - TC2: System light mode → Expect light theme (background ~#fbf1c7)\n  - TC3: Verify text colors → Dark: ~#ebdbb2, Light: ~#3c3836\n  - TC4: Verify accent colors → Consistent Gruvbox orange (#d65d0e)\n  - TC5: Toggle system preference → Expect theme updates\n* **Color Verification:** Use color picker tool to verify hex values\n* **Consistency:** Verify all UI elements use Gruvbox palette\n\nREQ: [BP009] - Blog Platform → Theme Toggle Control #N009\n* The system SHALL provide a visible toggle control for theme switching.\n* The toggle SHALL allow users to switch between dark and light themes.\n* Theme preference MAY be persisted using localStorage (JavaScript).\n* Theme toggle functionality SHALL degrade gracefully in JavaScript-disabled environments.\n* Theme preference SHALL persist across page navigation and browser sessions.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_009] - Blog Platform → Theme Toggle Test #BP009\n* **Objective:** Verify theme toggle functionality and persistence.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Locate theme toggle → Expect visible control on page\n  - TC2: Click toggle in dark mode → Expect switch to light mode\n  - TC3: Click toggle in light mode → Expect switch to dark mode\n  - TC4: Navigate to another page → Expect theme preference persists\n  - TC5: Refresh page → Expect theme preference persists\n  - TC6: Close and reopen browser → Expect theme preference persists\n* **Degradation:**\n  - TC7: Disable JavaScript → Expect page readable (system preference)\n  - TC8: Disable localStorage → Verify graceful handling\n* **Accessibility:** Verify toggle is keyboard accessible\n\nREQ: [BP010] - Blog Platform → Typography System #N010\n* The system SHALL use IBM Plex Sans font for body text.\n* The system SHALL use IBM Plex Sans font for headings.\n* The system SHALL use JetBrains Mono font for code blocks and monospace content.\n* Font files SHALL be served locally or via reliable CDN with fallback to system fonts.\n* **References:**\n  + [IBM Plex](https://www.ibm.com/plex/)\n  + [JetBrains Mono](https://www.jetbrains.com/lp/mono/)\n\nQA: [BP_QA_010] - Blog Platform → Typography Test #BP010\n* **Objective:** Verify correct fonts are applied.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Inspect body text → Expect IBM Plex Sans applied\n  - TC2: Inspect headings (h1-h6) → Expect IBM Plex Sans applied\n  - TC3: Inspect code blocks → Expect JetBrains Mono applied\n  - TC4: Inspect inline code → Expect JetBrains Mono applied\n  - TC5: Verify no system font fallback → Check computed styles\n  - TC6: Slow network test → Expect fonts load gracefully\n* **Rendering:** Verify legibility at various sizes (12px, 14px, 16px, 18px)\n* **Cross-browser:** Verify consistent font rendering\n\nREQ: [BP011] - Blog Platform → CSS Border Styling #N011\n* The system SHALL use CSS borders for terminal-inspired visual elements.\n* ASCII box-drawing characters (─, │, ┌, ┐, └, ┘) SHALL NOT be used for structural borders.\n* CSS-based borders ensure cross-browser compatibility and accessibility.\n* Border styling SHALL be consistent across themes (dark/light).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_011] - Blog Platform → CSS Border Styling Test #BP011\n* **Objective:** Verify borders use CSS, not ASCII characters.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Inspect border elements → Expect CSS border properties\n  - TC2: Search HTML source for box-drawing chars → Expect none found\n  - TC3: Verify borders render in CLI browsers → Expect readable\n  - TC4: Compare borders in dark/light themes → Expect consistent style\n* **Unicode Search:** Search for: ─ │ ┌ ┐ └ ┘ ├ ┤ ┬ ┴ ┼\n* **Inspection:** Use DevTools to verify border-style, border-width properties\n\nREQ: [BP012] - Blog Platform → Week Navigation Status Bar #N012\n* The system SHALL display a top status bar containing clickable week numbers.\n* Only completed weeks SHALL be displayed as clickable links.\n* Incomplete/upcoming weeks SHALL NOT be clickable.\n* Clicking a week number SHALL navigate to that week's blog post.\n* Week numbers SHALL be displayed in chronological order (1-52).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_012] - Blog Platform → Week Navigation Status Bar Test #BP012\n* **Objective:** Verify week navigation functionality in status bar.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Locate top status bar → Expect week numbers visible\n  - TC2: Verify completed weeks → Expect clickable links\n  - TC3: Verify upcoming weeks → Expect NOT clickable\n  - TC4: Click completed week number → Expect navigation to post\n  - TC5: Verify chronological order → Expect 1, 2, 3... 52\n  - TC6: Test all available week links → Expect correct destinations\n* **Boundary:** Test when only week 1 exists, when multiple weeks exist\n* **Visual:** Verify clickable/non-clickable states are visually distinct\n\nREQ: [BP013] - Blog Platform → Week Number Tooltips #N013\n* The system SHALL display native browser tooltips on hover over week numbers in the status bar.\n* Tooltips SHALL display the post title for the corresponding week.\n* Implementation SHALL use the HTML \`title\` attribute (native browser tooltip).\n* Custom JavaScript tooltip libraries SHALL NOT be used.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_013] - Blog Platform → Week Tooltips Test #BP013\n* **Objective:** Verify native tooltips show post titles on hover.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Hover over week number → Expect native browser tooltip appears\n  - TC2: Verify tooltip content → Expect post title displayed\n  - TC3: Test all available week tooltips → Expect correct titles\n  - TC4: Inspect HTML → Expect \`title\` attribute on link elements\n  - TC5: Verify no JS tooltip library → Check network requests, source\n* **Timing:** Tooltip should appear after standard browser delay (~500ms)\n\nREQ: [BP014] - Blog Platform → Weekly Index Navigation Link #N014\n* The system SHALL provide a \"Weeks\" label in the top status bar.\n* The \"Weeks\" label SHALL function as a link to the Weekly Index page.\n* The link SHALL navigate to \`/blog/weeks/\`.\n* The link SHALL be implemented as a standard anchor element (\`\u003ca\u003e\`) for CLI browser accessibility.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_014] - Blog Platform → Weekly Index Link Test #BP014\n* **Objective:** Verify \"Weeks\" label links to Weekly Index.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Locate \"Weeks\" label in status bar → Expect visible\n  - TC2: Click \"Weeks\" → Expect navigation to \`/blog/weeks/\`\n  - TC3: Inspect HTML → Expect standard \`\u003ca\u003e\` element\n  - TC4: Test in lynx → Expect link accessible and functional\n  - TC5: Test in w3m → Expect link accessible and functional\n* **Accessibility:** Verify link has appropriate aria-label if needed\n\nREQ: [BP015] - Blog Platform → Footer Navigation Bar #N015\n* The system SHALL display a bottom navigation bar on all pages.\n* Required navigation links: About, Weekly Index, Reports, RSS, and GitHub.\n* Links SHALL navigate to: \`/about/\`, \`/blog/weeks/\`, \`/blog/reports/\`, RSS feed URL, GitHub repository URL.\n* Navigation bar SHALL be consistent across all pages.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_015] - Blog Platform → Footer Navigation Test #BP015\n* **Objective:** Verify bottom navigation bar completeness and functionality.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Locate bottom navigation bar → Expect present on all pages\n  - TC2: Verify About link → Expect navigates to \`/about/\`\n  - TC3: Verify Weekly Index link → Expect navigates to \`/blog/weeks/\`\n  - TC4: Verify Reports link → Expect navigates to \`/blog/reports/\`\n  - TC5: Verify RSS link → Expect valid RSS feed URL\n  - TC6: Verify GitHub link → Expect GitHub repository URL\n* **Consistency:** Check navigation on blog index, post, about, community pages\n* **CLI Browsers:** Verify all links work in lynx, w3m\n\nREQ: [BP016] - Blog Platform → Accessible Navigation Labels #N016\n* All navigation links SHALL use descriptive text labels.\n* Icons MAY accompany text labels but SHALL NOT replace them.\n* Text labels ensure accessibility for screen readers and CLI browsers.\n* Link text SHALL be meaningful out of context (avoid \"click here\", \"read more\").\n\nQA: [BP_QA_016] - Blog Platform → Navigation Labels Test #BP016\n* **Objective:** Verify all navigation uses descriptive text.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Inspect all navigation elements → Expect descriptive text labels\n  - TC2: Verify icons accompany (not replace) text → If icons exist\n  - TC3: Test in CLI browser → Expect all nav understandable without visuals\n  - TC4: Screen reader test → Expect links announced with descriptive text\n  - TC5: Search for \"click here\", \"read more\" → Expect none in nav\n* **Accessibility:** Run axe audit on navigation elements\n\nREQ: [BP017] - Blog Platform → Table of Contents #N017\n* Each blog post SHALL display a table of contents at the top of the post content area.\n* The TOC SHALL list all major sections (h2, h3 headings) of the post.\n* TOC items SHALL be anchor links that navigate to the corresponding section.\n* TOC SHALL be generated automatically from post heading structure.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_017] - Blog Platform → Table of Contents Test #BP017\n* **Objective:** Verify TOC generation and navigation.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to post with 3+ headings → Expect TOC visible at top\n  - TC2: Verify all major sections listed → Expect h2, h3 headings present\n  - TC3: Click TOC item → Expect smooth scroll to section\n  - TC4: Verify anchor links → Expect URL hash updates (#section-id)\n  - TC5: Test in CLI browser → Expect anchor navigation works\n* **Boundary:** Test post with no headings, single heading, nested headings\n* **Content Types:** Test with code blocks in headings, special characters\n\nREQ: [BP018] - Blog Platform → Sticky Section Indicator #N018\n* Blog posts SHOULD display a sticky section indicator showing current reading position.\n* Indicator format example: \"§ Reading: Section Name\".\n* Implementation SHALL NOT require JavaScript.\n* This is a SHOULD requirement; graceful absence is acceptable.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_018] - Blog Platform → Section Indicator Test #BP018\n* **Objective:** Verify sticky section indicator (if implemented).\n* **Test Cases (if implemented):**\n  - TC1: Navigate to long post (5+ sections) → Expect indicator visible\n  - TC2: Scroll through sections → Expect indicator updates\n  - TC3: Verify format → Expect \"§ Reading: Section Name\" or similar\n  - TC4: Disable JavaScript → Expect indicator still works (CSS-only)\n  - TC5: Verify sticky behavior → Expect remains visible while scrolling\n* **Note:** SHOULD requirement; document if not implemented\n* **Implementation Check:** Verify pure CSS solution (scroll-snap, intersection)\n\nREQ: [BP019] - Blog Platform → About Page #N019\n* The system SHALL provide an About page at the URL \`/about/\`.\n* The About page SHALL describe the 52vibes project purpose and goals.\n* The About page SHALL include author/contributor information.\n* Page layout and styling SHALL be consistent with the rest of the site.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_019] - Blog Platform → About Page Test #BP019\n* **Objective:** Verify About page content and accessibility.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/about/\` → Expect HTTP 200, page loads\n  - TC2: Verify project description → Expect meaningful content\n  - TC3: Verify author information → Expect contributor details\n  - TC4: Verify layout consistency → Expect matches blog design\n  - TC5: Test in CLI browser → Expect content readable\n* **Content Quality:** Verify description explains 52vibes project\n* **SEO:** Verify meta tags present for about page\n\nREQ: [BP020] - Blog Platform → Weekly Index Page #N020\n* The system SHALL provide a Weekly Index page at \`/blog/weeks/\`.\n* The page SHALL display all 52 weeks in a tabular or list format.\n* Each week entry SHALL indicate status: completed, in-progress, or upcoming.\n* Completed weeks SHALL display post titles and link to the corresponding posts.\n* Upcoming weeks SHALL be visually distinguished and not linked.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_020] - Blog Platform → Weekly Index Page Test #BP020\n* **Objective:** Verify Weekly Index displays all 52 weeks correctly.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/blog/weeks/\` → Expect page loads\n  - TC2: Count week entries → Expect exactly 52 weeks listed\n  - TC3: Verify completed weeks → Expect title + link displayed\n  - TC4: Verify upcoming weeks → Expect not clickable, distinct styling\n  - TC5: Verify in-progress week → Expect distinguishable if present\n  - TC6: Click completed week link → Expect navigation to post\n* **CLI Browser:** Test table rendering in w3m (critical for tables)\n* **Responsive:** Verify table readable on mobile viewports\n\nREQ: [BP021] - Blog Platform → Reports Section #N021\n* The system SHALL provide a Reports section at \`/blog/reports/\`.\n* The section SHALL contain monthly and quarterly summary report posts.\n* Report listings SHALL display title, date, and type (monthly/quarterly).\n* An appropriate empty state message SHALL be displayed when no reports exist.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_021] - Blog Platform → Reports Section Test #BP021\n* **Objective:** Verify Reports section displays correctly.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/blog/reports/\` → Expect page loads\n  - TC2: Verify published monthly reports listed → When available\n  - TC3: Verify published quarterly reports listed → When available\n  - TC4: Click report link → Expect navigation to full report\n  - TC5: Verify empty state → When no reports exist, friendly message shown\n* **Content Types:** Verify both monthly and quarterly types distinguishable\n* **Ordering:** Verify reports ordered by date (most recent first)\n\nREQ: [BP022] - Blog Platform → Community Page #N022\n* The system SHALL provide a Community page at \`/community/\`.\n* The page SHALL display public GitHub repositories tagged with \"52vibes\".\n* JavaScript MAY be used to fetch repository data from the GitHub API.\n* Graceful fallback SHALL be provided when API is unavailable.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_022] - Blog Platform → Community Page Test #BP022\n* **Objective:** Verify Community page displays repositories.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/community/\` → Expect page loads\n  - TC2: If repos exist → Expect listed with information\n  - TC3: If no repos exist → Expect friendly message\n  - TC4: Verify JavaScript enabled → Expect API fetch works\n  - TC5: Test loading state → Expect visual feedback during fetch\n* **API Integration:** Verify correct GitHub API endpoint called\n* **Fallback:** Test behavior when API returns error\n\nREQ: [BP023] - Blog Platform → Blog Index Page #N023\n* The system SHALL provide a blog index at \`/blog/\`.\n* The index SHALL list all published blog posts.\n* Each listing SHALL display: title, publication date, and summary.\n* Posts SHALL be ordered with most recent first.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_023] - Blog Platform → Blog Index Test #BP023\n* **Objective:** Verify blog index lists all posts correctly.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/blog/\` → Expect page loads\n  - TC2: Verify all published posts listed → Expect complete list\n  - TC3: Verify each listing → Expect title, date, summary present\n  - TC4: Click post title → Expect navigation to full post\n  - TC5: Verify ordering → Expect most recent first\n  - TC6: Test pagination → If more than one page of posts\n* **Content:** Verify summary is truncated appropriately\n* **CLI Browser:** Verify list readable in lynx\n\nREQ: [BP024] - Blog Platform → Weekly Post URL Structure #N024\n* Weekly blog posts SHALL be accessible at URLs following the pattern \`/blog/week-XX-\u003ctitle\u003e/\`.\n* Example: \`/blog/week-01-infrastructure/\`.\n* Week number SHALL be zero-padded (01, 02, ... 52).\n* URL slug SHALL be derived from post title (lowercase, hyphenated).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_024] - Blog Platform → Weekly Post URL Test #BP024\n* **Objective:** Verify weekly post URL structure.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to weekly post → Verify URL matches pattern\n  - TC2: Verify URL format → \`/blog/week-XX-\u003ctitle\u003e/\`\n  - TC3: Verify zero-padding → Expect 01, 02, not 1, 2\n  - TC4: Test multiple weeks → Expect consistent pattern\n  - TC5: Verify slug format → Expect lowercase, hyphenated\n* **Boundary:** Test week-01, week-10, week-52\n* **Edge Cases:** Test titles with special characters, numbers\n\nREQ: [BP025] - Blog Platform → Monthly Report URL Structure #N025\n* Monthly report posts SHALL be accessible at URLs following the pattern \`/blog/reports/YYYY-MM/\`.\n* Example: \`/blog/reports/2026-01/\`.\n* Year and month SHALL be formatted as four-digit year and two-digit month.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_025] - Blog Platform → Monthly Report URL Test #BP025\n* **Objective:** Verify monthly report URL structure.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to monthly report → Verify URL matches pattern\n  - TC2: Verify URL format → \`/blog/reports/YYYY-MM/\`\n  - TC3: Verify date format → Four-digit year, two-digit month\n  - TC4: Example verification → \`/blog/reports/2026-01/\`\n* **Boundary:** Test January (01), December (12)\n* **Edge Cases:** Test year boundaries (2026-12 to 2027-01)\n\nREQ: [BP026] - Blog Platform → Quarterly Report URL Structure #N026\n* Quarterly report posts SHALL be accessible at URLs following the pattern \`/blog/reports/YYYY-qN/\`.\n* Example: \`/blog/reports/2026-q1/\`.\n* Quarter indicator SHALL be lowercase 'q' followed by quarter number (1-4).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_026] - Blog Platform → Quarterly Report URL Test #BP026\n* **Objective:** Verify quarterly report URL structure.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to quarterly report → Verify URL matches pattern\n  - TC2: Verify URL format → \`/blog/reports/YYYY-qN/\`\n  - TC3: Verify quarter indicator → Lowercase 'q' + 1-4\n  - TC4: Example verification → \`/blog/reports/2026-q1/\`\n* **Boundary:** Test q1, q2, q3, q4\n* **Case Sensitivity:** Verify lowercase 'q' (not 'Q')\n\nREQ: [BP027] - Blog Platform → Post Metadata Display #N027\n* Each blog post SHALL display the following metadata: title, publication date, estimated reading time, and quarter/theme indicator.\n* Quarter/theme indicator format: \"Q1: Agentic Infrastructure\" (or similar).\n* Metadata SHALL be prominently displayed near the top of the post.\n* Reading time SHOULD be calculated automatically from content length.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_027] - Blog Platform → Post Metadata Test #BP027\n* **Objective:** Verify post metadata is correctly displayed.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to blog post → Expect title displayed prominently\n  - TC2: Verify publication date → Expect human-readable format\n  - TC3: Verify reading time → Expect \"X min read\" format\n  - TC4: Verify quarter/theme → Expect \"Q1: Theme Name\" format\n  - TC5: Test multiple posts → Expect consistent metadata display\n* **Calculation:** Verify reading time is reasonable for content length\n* **Consistency:** Compare metadata display across different posts\n\nREQ: [BP028] - Blog Platform → Previous/Next Post Navigation #N028\n* Each blog post SHALL provide navigation links to adjacent week posts.\n* \"Previous week\" link SHALL navigate to the prior week's post.\n* \"Next week\" link SHALL navigate to the following week's post.\n* Links SHALL NOT appear when not applicable (no Previous for Week 1, no Next for latest).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_028] - Blog Platform → Post Navigation Test #BP028\n* **Objective:** Verify previous/next post navigation.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to middle week → Expect both Previous and Next links\n  - TC2: Click Previous link → Expect navigation to prior week\n  - TC3: Click Next link → Expect navigation to following week\n  - TC4: Navigate to Week 1 → Expect no Previous link\n  - TC5: Navigate to latest week → Expect no Next link\n  - TC6: Follow complete chain → Expect all weeks reachable\n* **Boundary:** Test first week, last published week, middle week\n* **Edge Case:** Single published week (no navigation links)\n\nREQ: [BP029] - Blog Platform → Session Log Links #N029\n* Each blog post SHALL include a link to the corresponding session log on the GitHub Wiki.\n* The link SHALL be clearly labeled (e.g., \"View Session Log\").\n* The link SHALL navigate to the wiki page containing that week's collaboration data.\n* This connects polished blog content to raw human-AI collaboration artifacts.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_029] - Blog Platform → Session Log Links Test #BP029\n* **Objective:** Verify session log links connect to GitHub Wiki.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to blog post → Expect session log link visible\n  - TC2: Verify link label → Expect descriptive (e.g., \"View Session Log\")\n  - TC3: Click session log link → Expect opens GitHub Wiki page\n  - TC4: Verify wiki content → Expect session data for that week\n  - TC5: Test multiple posts → Expect each links to correct wiki page\n* **Cross-reference:** Verify wiki page title matches week number\n* **External Link:** Verify link opens in appropriate context\n\nREQ: [BP030] - Blog Platform → Repository/Code Links #N030\n* Each blog post SHALL include a link to the corresponding GitHub repository or code artifacts.\n* The link SHALL be clearly labeled.\n* The link SHALL navigate to the week's relevant code location.\n* This enables readers to explore actual code produced during the week.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_030] - Blog Platform → Repository Links Test #BP030\n* **Objective:** Verify repository/code links are functional.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to blog post → Expect code/repository link visible\n  - TC2: Verify link label → Expect descriptive text\n  - TC3: Click repository link → Expect opens GitHub repository\n  - TC4: Verify linked content → Expect corresponds to week's project\n  - TC5: Test multiple posts → Expect each links to correct repository\n* **Link Validity:** Verify links are not broken (HTTP 200)\n* **Content Match:** Verify repository content matches week's topic\n\nREQ: [BP031] - Blog Platform → RSS/Atom Feed #N037\n* The system SHALL provide an RSS or Atom feed for blog subscribers.\n* Feed SHALL be accessible at a standard location (e.g., \`/index.xml\` or \`/blog/index.xml\`).\n* Feed SHALL include all published blog posts.\n* Feed SHALL be valid according to RSS/Atom specifications.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_031] - Blog Platform → RSS Feed Test #BP031\n* **Objective:** Verify RSS/Atom feed validity and content.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to feed URL → Expect valid XML response\n  - TC2: Verify feed format → Expect valid RSS or Atom structure\n  - TC3: Verify recent posts included → Expect published posts in feed\n  - TC4: Test in RSS reader → Expect feed parseable\n  - TC5: Validate with W3C Feed Validation Service → Expect no errors\n* **Content:** Verify each item has title, link, description, pubDate\n* **Encoding:** Verify proper character encoding (UTF-8)\n* **References:**\n  + [W3C Feed Validator](https://validator.w3.org/feed/)\n\nREQ: [BP032] - Blog Platform → Basic Meta Tags #N038\n* Each page SHALL include appropriate meta tags for SEO.\n* Required meta tags: \`\u003ctitle\u003e\`, \`\u003cmeta name=\"description\"\u003e\`.\n* Meta description SHALL be relevant to page content.\n* Title tag SHALL contain meaningful page title.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_032] - Blog Platform → Basic Meta Tags Test #BP032\n* **Objective:** Verify SEO meta tags on all pages.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: View page source → Expect \`\u003ctitle\u003e\` tag present\n  - TC2: Verify title content → Expect contains post/page title\n  - TC3: Verify description meta → Expect \`\u003cmeta name=\"description\"\u003e\` present\n  - TC4: Verify description content → Expect relevant to page\n* **Page Types:** Test on blog index, blog post, about, reports, community\n* **Length:** Verify description is appropriate length (50-160 chars)\n* **Uniqueness:** Verify each page has unique title/description\n\nREQ: [BP033] - Blog Platform → Open Graph Meta Tags #N039\n* Each page SHALL include Open Graph meta tags for social media sharing.\n* Required tags: \`og:title\`, \`og:description\`, \`og:image\`, \`og:url\`, \`og:type\`.\n* Blog posts SHALL use \`og:type\` of \"article\".\n* Tags enable rich previews when shared on social media platforms.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_033] - Blog Platform → Open Graph Tags Test #BP033\n* **Objective:** Verify Open Graph meta tags for social sharing.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: View page source → Expect \`og:title\` meta tag present\n  - TC2: Verify og:description → Expect meta tag with content\n  - TC3: Verify og:image → Expect social card URL\n  - TC4: Verify og:url → Expect canonical URL\n  - TC5: Verify og:type → Expect \"article\" for blog posts\n  - TC6: Test with Facebook Sharing Debugger → Expect preview renders\n* **Image:** Verify og:image URL is valid and accessible\n* **References:**\n  + [Facebook Sharing Debugger](https://developers.facebook.com/tools/debug/)\n\nREQ: [BP034] - Blog Platform → Twitter Card Meta Tags #N040\n* Each page SHALL include Twitter Card meta tags for Twitter sharing previews.\n* Required tags: \`twitter:card\`, \`twitter:title\`, \`twitter:description\`, \`twitter:image\`.\n* Card type SHALL be \"summary_large_image\" for visual impact.\n* Tags enable rich previews when shared on Twitter/X.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_034] - TC3: Verify twitter:title → Expect meta tag with content\n  - TC4: Verify twitter:description → Expect meta tag with content\n  - TC5: Verify twitter:image → Expect image URL\n  - TC6: Test with Twitter Card Validator → Expect preview renders\n* **Image Dimensions:** Verify image meets Twitter requirements\n* **References:**\n  + [Twitter Card Validator](https://cards-dev.twitter.com/validator)\n\nREQ: [BP035] - Blog Platform → XML Sitemap #N041\n* The system SHALL generate and publish an XML sitemap for search engine indexing.\n* Sitemap SHALL be accessible at \`/sitemap.xml\`.\n* Sitemap SHALL include all blog posts, static pages, and report pages.\n* Sitemap entries SHALL include \`lastmod\` dates for accurate crawling.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_035] - TC3: Inspect DOM → Expect \`\u003cmain\u003e\` wraps primary content\n  - TC4: Inspect DOM → Expect \`\u003carticle\u003e\` wraps blog post content\n  - TC5: Inspect DOM → Expect \`\u003cfooter\u003e\` for page footer\n  - TC6: Validate HTML5 → Expect no structural errors\n* **Hierarchy:** Verify heading levels (h1, h2, h3) are logical\n* **Tools:** W3C HTML Validator, axe accessibility checker\n\nREQ: [BP041] - Blog Platform → Image Alt Text #N047\n* All images SHALL include descriptive alt text via the \`alt\` attribute.\n* Alt text SHALL be meaningful and contextually appropriate.\n* Decorative images MAY use empty alt text (\`alt=\"\"\`).\n* Alt text ensures accessibility for screen reader users.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_041] - TC5: Check link contrast → Expect distinguishable from surrounding text\n  - TC6: Check code block contrast → Expect readable in both themes\n* **Tools:** axe DevTools, WAVE, Colour Contrast Analyser\n* **Manual Check:** Verify UI is readable for color-blind users\n\nREQ: [BP045] - * **TOOL**: `{"content":"# Week 1: Requirements - crush-export Tool (CX)\n\n\n\n\n## Product Overview\n\n**Product Name:** crush-export Tool  \n**Product ID:** CX  \n**Description:** Command-line utility written in Go that extracts session data from the Crush AI agent's SQLite database (\`.crush/crush.db\`) and generates wiki-ready markdown documents for publication.\n\n**Installation:** \`cd crush-export \u0026\u0026 go build -o crush-export ./cmd/crush-export\`\n\n---\n\n## Requirements\n\n\nREQ: [CX001] - crush-export → Session Data Processing #N035\n* The tool SHALL read session data from the Crush SQLite database (\`.crush/crush.db\`).\n* The tool SHALL generate wiki-ready markdown documents from session data.\n* Output format SHALL be compatible with GitHub Wiki publishing.\n* The tool SHALL be implemented in Go programming language.\n* Command-line interface SHALL support listing sessions and exporting to files.\n\nQA: [CX_QA_001] - crush-export → Session Processing Test #CX001\n* **Objective:** Verify session data extraction from SQLite.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Verify \`.crush/crush.db\` exists → Expect SQLite database present\n  - TC2: Run \`./crush-export -l\` → Expect sessions listed with IDs\n  - TC3: Run \`./crush-export -db .crush/crush.db -out sessions/\` → Expect markdown files generated\n  - TC4: Verify output format → Expect valid markdown syntax\n  - TC5: Verify wiki compatibility → Expect renderable in GitHub Wiki\n* **Build Verification:** \`cd crush-export \u0026\u0026 go build -o crush-export ./cmd/crush-export\`\n* **Empty Database:** Test with database containing no sessions\n\nREQ: [CX002] - crush-export → Metadata Extraction #N036\n* The tool SHALL extract session metadata including: duration, message count, files created/modified, and error count.\n* Metadata SHALL be included in the generated markdown document.\n* Statistics section SHALL be prominently placed in the output.\n* Accuracy of metadata SHALL be verified against raw session data.\n\nQA: [CX_QA_002] - crush-export → Metadata Extraction Test #CX002\n* **Objective:** Verify session metadata is correctly extracted.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Run export on known session → Examine output markdown\n  - TC2: Verify duration field → Expect session duration included\n  - TC3: Verify message count → Expect total message count included\n  - TC4: Verify files modified count → Expect files created/modified count\n  - TC5: Verify error count → Expect error count included\n* **Boundary Cases:**\n  - BC1: Empty session (no messages) → Expect graceful handling\n  - BC2: Single-message session → Expect minimal output\n  - BC3: Long session (100+ messages) → Expect complete processing\n* **Accuracy:** Cross-reference metadata with database query results\n\nREQ: [CX003] - crush-export → Document Structure #N032\n* The generated markdown document SHALL include the following sections:\n  - \"Lessons Learned\" section (placeholder for human curation)\n  - Session statistics section\n  - Key conversation excerpts section\n  - Full conversation log section\n* Section ordering SHALL follow the specified hierarchy.\n* Full conversation log MAY use collapsible sections for readability.\n\nQA: [CX_QA_003] - * **USER**: ### 1. Static Site Generator & Hosting
  
   * Hugo version? Which version should the technical requirements target? (e.g.,  v0.120+  for specific features)
    **ANSWER**: The latest version, unless you have a strong reason to use a older version.
   * Cloudflare Pages build settings? Node version, environment variables, build command customizations?
    **ANSWER**: I want to avoid NPM. But if absolutely needed, use latest version. For now no customizations. Env. variables - you can use whatever required. Make sure you document all of them.
   * Custom domain DNS setup? Is `52vibes.dev` already configured? Is it Cloudflare-managed or external DNS?
    **ANSWER**: I only bought the domain from Cloudflare. Nothing has been configured. If you cannot do it yourself, tell me what needs to be done and I'll do it.
  
  ### 2. Theme Architecture
  
   * Theme toggle mechanism? CSS-only via  prefers-color-scheme  + JS enhancement, or JS-required toggle? Should this use CSS custom properties for runtime switching?
    **ANSWER**: CSS + JS enhancement (if required for persistence). I want to minimize JS usage as much as possible.
   * Font loading strategy? Self-hosted fonts, Google Fonts CDN, or Cloudflare Fonts? Subset fonts for performance?
    **ANSWER**: Google Fonts CDN is preferred. But if you have a strong reason to self-host them, design and implement things accordingly. If you need me to do anything, be specific and tell me.
   * Build-time vs runtime social cards? Generate images at build time (Hugo image processing) or use a serverless function?
    **ANSWER**: I don't want to run any server-side logic since I don't want to incur additional cost to run my blog.
  
  ### 3. Community Page Architecture
  
   * GitHub API rate limiting strategy? Public unauthenticated calls (60/hour) vs authenticated. Client-side vs buildi-time fetch?
    **ANSWER**: I am not going to copy auth material into a client facing page. So, unauthenticated API is the only choice.
   * Caching approach? localStorage, sessionStorage, HTTP caching headers?
    **ANSWER**: You choose. Give clear reasons for your choice.
  
  ### 4. Accessibility & CLI Browser Support
  
   * Minimum WCAG compliance level? AA (standard) or AAA (enhanced)?
    **ANSWER**: 2.2 at level AA. But if you can hit AAA, go for it.
   * Priority CLI browser? lynx (most restrictive) or w3m (better table support)?
    **ANSWER**: I would test against both. So it should render on both .If table support is a problem, be smart and figure out how to publish content to be able to work with both browsers.

TS4: Verify Cloudflare proxy status → Expect orange cloud enabled in dashboard\n* **Boundary Cases:**\n  - BC1: Test immediately after DNS change → Document propagation time\n  - BC2: Test from different ISPs → Expect consistent results after propagation\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_CFP_0001] - Blog Platform → Cloudflare Pages Project Configuration #BP001\n* A Cloudflare Pages project SHALL be created and linked to the GitHub repository.\n* Build configuration SHALL specify:\n  - Build command: \`hugo --minify\`\n  - Build output directory: \`public\`\n  - Root directory: \`/\` (repository root)\n  - Hugo version environment variable: \`HUGO_VERSION=0.139.0\`\n* Production branch SHALL be set to \`main\`.\n* Preview deployments SHALL be enabled for pull requests.\n* The project name SHALL result in a \`*.pages.dev\` URL that serves the site.\n* References:\n  + [Cloudflare Pages Hugo Framework Guide](https://developers.cloudflare.com/pages/framework-guides/deploy-a-hugo-site/)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_CFP_TEST_0001] - Blog Platform → Cloudflare Pages Build Verification #BP_CFP_0001\n* **Objective:** Verify Cloudflare Pages builds and deploys successfully.\n* **Setup:** Link GitHub repository to Cloudflare Pages project.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Push commit to main branch → Expect build triggers automatically\n  - TS2: Monitor build logs → Expect Hugo build completes without errors\n  - TS3: Verify build output → Expect \`public/\` directory generated\n  - TS4: Access \`\u003cproject\u003e.pages.dev\` → Expect site accessible\n  - TS5: Verify HUGO_VERSION in build → Expect version 0.139.0 or higher\n* **Failure Cases:**\n  - FC1: Invalid Hugo config → Expect build fails with clear error\n  - FC2: Missing theme → Expect build fails, previous deployment remains live\n* **Performance:**\n  - Measure build duration → Expect under 2 minutes for initial build\n  - Measure deployment time → Expect under 1 minute after build\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_CFP_0002] - Blog Platform → Environment Variables #BP001\n* The following environment variables SHALL be configured in Cloudflare Pages:\n  - \`HUGO_VERSION\`: \`0.139.0\` (or latest stable)\n  - \`HUGO_ENVIRONMENT\`: \`production\` (for production builds)\n* Environment variables SHALL be set in Cloudflare Pages project settings.\n* No sensitive credentials SHALL be stored in environment variables for this project.\n* References:\n  + [Cloudflare Pages Environment Variables](https://developers.cloudflare.com/pages/configuration/build-configuration/#environment-variables)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_CFP_TEST_0002] - Blog Platform → Environment Variable Verification #BP_CFP_0002\n* **Objective:** Verify environment variables are correctly applied.\n* **Setup:** Configure environment variables in Cloudflare Pages dashboard.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Trigger build → Inspect build logs for HUGO_VERSION\n  - TS2: Verify Hugo version in output → Expect matches configured version\n  - TS3: Check production environment → Expect HUGO_ENVIRONMENT=production\n* **Verification:**\n  - Build log SHALL show \"Hugo v0.139.0\" or configured version\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_HUGO_0001] - Blog Platform → Hugo Base URL Configuration #BP001\n* Hugo configuration SHALL set \`baseURL\` to \`https://52vibes.dev/\`.\n* Hugo configuration file SHALL be \`hugo.toml\` (TOML format preferred).\n* The blog section SHALL be configured to serve content from \`/blog/\` path.\n* Configuration SHALL include:\n  - \`languageCode\`: \`en-us\`\n  - \`title\`: \`52 Vibes\`\n  - \`enableRobotsTXT\`: \`true\`\n  - \`enableGitInfo\`: \`true\` (for lastmod dates)\n* References:\n  + [Hugo Configuration](https://gohugo.io/getting-started/configuration/)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_HUGO_TEST_0001] - Blog Platform → Base URL and Path Verification #BP_HUGO_0001\n* **Objective:** Verify Hugo generates correct URLs and paths.\n* **Setup:** Build site locally with \`hugo --minify\`.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Inspect generated HTML → Expect all URLs use \`https://52vibes.dev/\`\n  - TS2: Verify blog index path → Expect accessible at \`/blog/\`\n  - TS3: Check canonical URLs → Expect \`\u003clink rel=\"canonical\"\u003e\` uses correct base\n  - TS4: Verify internal links → Expect no broken internal links\n  - TS5: Check sitemap.xml → Expect all URLs use production base URL\n* **Local vs Production:**\n  - Local development MAY use \`localhost:1313\`\n  - Production build MUST use \`https://52vibes.dev/\`\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_SSL_0001] - Blog Platform → HTTPS and SSL Configuration #BP001\n* All traffic SHALL be served over HTTPS.\n* HTTP requests SHALL redirect to HTTPS (301 permanent redirect).\n* SSL certificate SHALL be automatically provisioned by Cloudflare.\n* SSL mode SHALL be set to \"Full (strict)\" in Cloudflare settings.\n* HSTS (HTTP Strict Transport Security) SHOULD be enabled.\n* References:\n  + [Cloudflare SSL/TLS](https://developers.cloudflare.com/ssl/)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_SSL_TEST_0001] - Blog Platform → HTTPS and Certificate Verification #BP_SSL_0001\n* **Objective:** Verify SSL/TLS is correctly configured.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Request \`http://52vibes.dev/blog\` → Expect 301 redirect to HTTPS\n  - TS2: Request \`https://52vibes.dev/blog\` → Expect HTTP 200\n  - TS3: Inspect certificate → Expect valid, issued by Cloudflare\n  - TS4: Check certificate expiry → Expect auto-renewal configured\n  - TS5: Test with SSL Labs → Expect A or A+ rating\n* **Security Headers:**\n  - Verify HSTS header present (if enabled)\n  - Check for secure cookies (if any)\n* **References:**\n  + [SSL Labs Server Test](https://www.ssllabs.com/ssltest/)\n\n### Core Architecture (BP002, BP003, BP004)\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_SSR_0001] - Blog Platform → Server-Side Rendering Architecture #BP002\n* All page content SHALL be rendered at build time by Hugo (Static Site Generation).\n* HTML output SHALL contain complete content without requiring JavaScript hydration.\n* No client-side templating frameworks (React, Vue, etc.) SHALL be used.\n* Hugo templates SHALL use Go template syntax for content rendering.\n* Template directory structure SHALL follow Hugo conventions:\n  - \`layouts/_default/baseof.html\` - base template\n  - \`layouts/_default/single.html\` - single content pages\n  - \`layouts/_default/list.html\` - list/index pages\n  - \`layouts/partials/\` - reusable template components\n* References:\n  + [Hugo Templates](https://gohugo.io/templates/)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_SSR_TEST_0001] - Blog Platform → Static Rendering Verification #BP_SSR_0001\n* **Objective:** Verify all content is statically rendered.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Build site with \`hugo --minify\` → Inspect \`public/\` directory\n  - TS2: Open any HTML file → Expect complete content in source\n  - TS3: Disable JavaScript in browser → Load page → Expect all content visible\n  - TS4: Use \`curl\` to fetch page → Expect complete HTML in response\n  - TS5: Check for hydration scripts → Expect none present\n* **Content Types:**\n  - Test blog post pages\n  - Test index/list pages\n  - Test static pages (About, etc.)\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_NOJS_0001] - Blog Platform → JavaScript Budget and Constraints #BP002\n* Total JavaScript payload SHALL NOT exceed 2KB (minified, uncompressed).\n* JavaScript SHALL be used ONLY for:\n  - Theme toggle persistence (localStorage) - ~500 bytes\n  - Community page GitHub API fetch - ~1KB\n* No JavaScript frameworks or libraries SHALL be included.\n* All JavaScript SHALL be inline (no external JS files) or in a single bundled file.\n* JavaScript SHALL use vanilla ES6+ syntax (no transpilation required for modern browsers).\n* References:\n  + [JavaScript Module Best Practices](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Guide/Modules)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_NOJS_TEST_0001] - Blog Platform → JavaScript Budget Verification #BP_NOJS_0001\n* **Objective:** Verify JavaScript stays within budget.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Build production site → Locate all JavaScript in output\n  - TS2: Measure total JS size → Expect ≤2KB minified\n  - TS3: List all JS functionality → Expect only theme toggle + API fetch\n  - TS4: Check for framework code → Expect none (React, Vue, jQuery, etc.)\n  - TS5: Verify ES6+ syntax → Expect no transpilation artifacts\n* **Tools:**\n  - Use browser DevTools Network tab\n  - Use \`wc -c\` on minified JS files\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_GRACE_0001] - Blog Platform → Graceful Degradation Strategy #BP002\n* When JavaScript is disabled:\n  - Theme SHALL default to system preference via \`prefers-color-scheme\`\n  - Theme toggle control SHALL remain visible but non-functional\n  - Community page SHALL display fallback link to GitHub topics page\n* No \"JavaScript required\" messages SHALL be displayed.\n* No broken layouts or missing content SHALL occur without JavaScript.\n* All navigation SHALL remain fully functional without JavaScript.\n* References:\n  + [Progressive Enhancement](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Glossary/Progressive_Enhancement)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_GRACE_TEST_0001] - Blog Platform → Graceful Degradation Verification #BP_GRACE_0001\n* **Objective:** Verify site functions correctly without JavaScript.\n* **Setup:** Disable JavaScript in browser settings.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Load blog index → Expect all posts listed, readable\n  - TS2: Navigate between pages → Expect all links work\n  - TS3: Check theme → Expect matches system preference\n  - TS4: View theme toggle → Expect visible (may be non-functional)\n  - TS5: Load Community page → Expect fallback content/link displayed\n  - TS6: Check for error messages → Expect none\n* **Browsers:**\n  - Test in Chrome, Firefox with JS disabled\n  - Test in lynx (inherently no JS)\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_RESP_0001] - Blog Platform → Responsive Breakpoint System #BP003\n* CSS SHALL implement the following breakpoint system:\n  - Mobile: \`max-width: 767px\`\n  - Tablet: \`min-width: 768px\` and \`max-width: 1023px\`\n  - Desktop: \`min-width: 1024px\`\n  - Large Desktop: \`min-width: 1440px\` (optional enhancement)\n* Breakpoints SHALL be defined as CSS custom properties or SCSS variables.\n* Mobile-first approach SHALL be used (base styles for mobile, media queries for larger).\n* No horizontal scrolling SHALL occur at any viewport width ≥320px.\n* References:\n  + [CSS Media Queries](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/CSS_media_queries)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_RESP_TEST_0001] - Blog Platform → Breakpoint Behavior Verification #BP_RESP_0001\n* **Objective:** Verify responsive behavior at all breakpoints.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Set viewport to 320px width → Expect no horizontal scroll, content readable\n  - TS2: Set viewport to 375px width → Expect mobile layout\n  - TS3: Set viewport to 768px width → Expect tablet layout transition\n  - TS4: Set viewport to 1024px width → Expect desktop layout\n  - TS5: Set viewport to 1920px width → Expect full desktop layout\n  - TS6: Resize viewport dynamically → Expect smooth transitions\n* **Orientation:**\n  - Test mobile viewports in portrait and landscape\n* **Content Types:**\n  - Test with long code blocks\n  - Test with tables\n  - Test with images\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_RESP_0002] - Blog Platform → Fluid Typography and Spacing #BP003\n* Typography SHALL scale fluidly using CSS \`clamp()\` function.\n* Base font size range: \`clamp(16px, 2.5vw, 18px)\` for body text.\n* Heading sizes SHALL scale proportionally.\n* Spacing (margins, padding) SHALL use relative units (rem, em) or viewport units.\n* Line length SHALL be constrained to 65-75 characters for readability.\n* References:\n  + [CSS clamp()](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/clamp)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_RESP_TEST_0002] - Blog Platform → Typography Scaling Verification #BP_RESP_0002\n* **Objective:** Verify typography scales appropriately.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Inspect body font size at 320px viewport → Expect ~16px\n  - TS2: Inspect body font size at 1920px viewport → Expect ~18px\n  - TS3: Measure line length in characters → Expect 65-75 characters max\n  - TS4: Check heading hierarchy → Expect proportional scaling\n  - TS5: Verify relative units in CSS → Expect rem/em usage\n* **Readability:**\n  - Verify text is readable at all viewport sizes\n  - Verify adequate spacing between elements\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_PERF_0001] - Blog Platform → Asset Optimization Pipeline #BP004\n* Hugo asset pipeline SHALL be configured for optimization:\n  - CSS: Minification enabled, unused CSS removal (if using SCSS)\n  - HTML: Minification via \`hugo --minify\`\n  - Images: WebP conversion with fallback, responsive srcset generation\n* Total page weight targets:\n  - Blog index: ≤500KB\n  - Blog post (without images): ≤300KB\n  - Any page with images: ≤800KB\n* Asset fingerprinting SHALL be enabled for cache busting.\n* References:\n  + [Hugo Asset Minification](https://gohugo.io/hugo-pipes/minification/)\n  + [Hugo Image Processing](https://gohugo.io/content-management/image-processing/)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_PERF_TEST_0001] - Blog Platform → Asset Optimization Verification #BP_PERF_0001\n* **Objective:** Verify assets are properly optimized.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Build with \`hugo --minify\` → Verify minification applied\n  - TS2: Inspect CSS output → Expect minified (no whitespace/comments)\n  - TS3: Inspect HTML output → Expect minified\n  - TS4: Check image formats → Expect WebP with fallbacks\n  - TS5: Measure page weights → Verify within budget\n  - TS6: Check asset URLs → Expect fingerprinted filenames\n* **Tools:**\n  - Use browser DevTools Network tab for size measurements\n  - Use \`du -h\` on output files\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_PERF_0002] - Blog Platform → Core Web Vitals Optimization #BP004\n* Largest Contentful Paint (LCP) SHALL be under 2.5 seconds.\n* First Input Delay (FID) SHALL be under 100ms.\n* Cumulative Layout Shift (CLS) SHALL be under 0.1.\n* First Contentful Paint (FCP) SHOULD be under 1.5 seconds.\n* Implementation strategies:\n  - Preload critical fonts\n  - Inline critical CSS\n  - Defer non-critical resources\n  - Reserve space for dynamic content (prevent layout shifts)\n* References:\n  + [Core Web Vitals](https://web.dev/vitals/)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_PERF_TEST_0002] - Blog Platform → Core Web Vitals Measurement #BP_PERF_0002\n* **Objective:** Verify Core Web Vitals meet targets.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Run Lighthouse on blog index → Expect Performance ≥95\n  - TS2: Measure LCP → Expect \u003c2.5s\n  - TS3: Measure FID → Expect \u003c100ms\n  - TS4: Measure CLS → Expect \u003c0.1\n  - TS5: Measure FCP → Expect \u003c1.5s\n  - TS6: Run on multiple page types → Expect consistent scores\n* **Testing Conditions:**\n  - Test with throttled connection (Slow 4G)\n  - Test with CPU throttling (4x slowdown)\n* **Tools:**\n  - Chrome DevTools Lighthouse\n  - WebPageTest.org\n  - PageSpeed Insights\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_PERF_0003] - Blog Platform → Font Loading Strategy #BP004\n* Fonts SHALL be loaded from Google Fonts CDN.\n* Font loading SHALL use \`font-display: swap\` to prevent invisible text.\n* Font preconnect hints SHALL be included in \`\u003chead\u003e\`:\n  - \`\u003clink rel=\"preconnect\" href=\"https://fonts.googleapis.com\"\u003e\`\n  - \`\u003clink rel=\"preconnect\" href=\"https://fonts.gstatic.com\" crossorigin\u003e\`\n* Font families to load:\n  - IBM Plex Sans: weights 400, 500, 600, 700\n  - JetBrains Mono: weight 400\n* Font subsetting SHOULD be applied (latin subset only for initial load).\n* References:\n  + [Google Fonts CSS API](https://developers.google.com/fonts/docs/css2)\n  + [font-display](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/@font-face/font-display)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_PERF_TEST_0003] - Blog Platform → Font Loading Verification #BP_PERF_0003\n* **Objective:** Verify fonts load efficiently without blocking render.\n* **Test Steps:**\n  - TS1: Inspect \`\u003chead\u003e\` → Expect preconnect hints for Google Fonts\n  - TS2: Check font-display → Expect \`swap\` in font declarations\n  - TS3: Block Google Fonts → Expect fallback fonts display immediately\n  - TS4: Measure font load time → Expect \u003c500ms on fast connection\n  - TS5: Check for FOIT (Flash of Invisible Text) → Expect none\n  - TS6: Check for FOUT (Flash of Unstyled Text) → Acceptable with swap\n* **Network Tab:**\n  - Verify font files loaded from fonts.gstatic.com\n  - Verify only required weights loaded\n","id":"20260105125854","path":"./notes/20260105125854/README.md","project":"52vibes","title":"Week 1: Technical Requirements - Blog Platform (BP-TECH)"}`

* **TOOL**: `{"content":"# Week 1: Technical Requirements - Blog Platform (BP-TECH)\n\n\n\n\n## Product Overview\n\n**Product Name:** Blog Platform  \n**Product ID:** BP  \n**Technical Spec ID:** BP-TECH  \n**Description:** Technical architecture and implementation requirements for the static blog site built with Hugo, deployed to Cloudflare Pages.\n\n---\n\n## Technical Decisions\n\n| Decision Area | Choice | Rationale |\n|---------------|--------|-----------|\n| Static Site Generator | Hugo v0.139+ (extended) | Latest features, SCSS support, image processing |\n| Hosting Platform | Cloudflare Pages | Native Hugo support, global CDN, free tier |\n| Theme System | CSS custom properties + prefers-color-scheme | Minimal JS, instant theme switching |\n| Font Loading | Google Fonts with font-display: swap | CDN reliability, performance optimization |\n| Social Cards | Hugo image processing (build-time) | No runtime cost, static assets |\n| Community API Caching | localStorage (5-min TTL) | Cross-session persistence, reduced API calls |\n| CLI Browser Support | Semantic HTML + progressive enhancement | Works in lynx (strict) and w3m (tables) |\n| Accessibility | WCAG 2.2 Level AA (target AAA) | Inclusive design standard |\n\n---\n\n## Technical Requirements\n\n### Infrastructure \u0026 Deployment (BP001, BP005)\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_DNS_0001] - TS5: Check for hydration scripts → Expect none present\n* **Content Types:**\n  - Test blog post pages\n  - Test index/list pages\n  - Test static pages (About, etc.)\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_NOJS_0001] - Blog Platform → JavaScript Budget and Constraints #BP002\n* Total JavaScript payload SHALL NOT exceed 2KB (minified, uncompressed).\n* JavaScript SHALL be used ONLY for:\n  - Theme toggle persistence (localStorage) - ~500 bytes\n  - Community page GitHub API fetch - ~1KB\n* No JavaScript frameworks or libraries SHALL be included.\n* All JavaScript SHALL be inline (no external JS files) or in a single bundled file.\n* JavaScript SHALL use vanilla ES6+ syntax (no transpilation required for modern browsers).\n* References:\n  + [JavaScript Module Best Practices](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Guide/Modules)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_NOJS_TEST_0001] - TS2: Measure total JS size → Expect ≤2KB minified\n  - TS3: List all JS functionality → Expect only theme toggle + API fetch\n  - TS4: Check for framework code → Expect none (React, Vue, jQuery, etc.)\n  - TS5: Verify ES6+ syntax → Expect no transpilation artifacts\n* **Tools:**\n  - Use browser DevTools Network tab\n  - Use \`wc -c\` on minified JS files\n\nTECH_REQ: [BP_GRACE_0001] - Blog Platform → Graceful Degradation Strategy #BP002\n* When JavaScript is disabled:\n  - Theme SHALL default to system preference via \`prefers-color-scheme\`\n  - Theme toggle control SHALL remain visible but non-functional\n  - Community page SHALL display fallback link to GitHub topics page\n* No \"JavaScript required\" messages SHALL be displayed.\n* No broken layouts or missing content SHALL occur without JavaScript.\n* All navigation SHALL remain fully functional without JavaScript.\n* References:\n  + [Progressive Enhancement](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Glossary/Progressive_Enhancement)\n\nSYSTEST: [BP_GRACE_TEST_0001] -
